## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators and damping/forcing models)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the time-derivative of velocity (acceleration), typical of oscillator ODEs written in state-space form. With only t and v available, plausible governing structures are velocity-dependent damping/friction and time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation rather than position-dependent restoring forces.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear viscous damping (free decay in velocity coordinate): dv_dt = -c0 * v
- Affine drag with bias (constant acceleration plus linear resistance): dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v
- Quadratic/turbulent drag (high-Reynolds drag surrogate): dv_dt = -c0 * v * Abs(v)
- Cubic (Rayleigh-type) nonlinear damping / self-excitation: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3
- General odd-polynomial velocity nonlinearity (nonlinear dissipation/actuation fit): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5
- General polynomial in v (allows asymmetric effects): dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**2 + c3 * v**3
- Dry (Coulomb) friction idealization: dv_dt = -c0 * sign(v)
- Smooth dry-friction (Stribeck-like regularization): dv_dt = -c0 * tanh(c1 * v)
- Additive harmonic forcing with viscous damping (driven oscillator reduced form): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)
- Parametrically modulated damping (time-varying dissipation): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t + c3)) * v
- Nonlinear self-excitation plus periodic drive (limit-cycle under forcing): dv_dt = (c0 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4)
- Impulsive/kick forcing in time (transient excitation): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * exp(-c2 * (t - c3)**2)
- Slowly varying/ramped forcing (nonstationary operating condition): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * t + c2 * t**2
- State-dependent gain on periodic drive (velocity–forcing coupling): dv_dt = -c0 * v + c1 * v * sin(c2 * t + c3)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd symmetry in v (terms like v, v**3, v*Abs(v)) typically represents direction-opposing damping or direction-aligned self-excitation; even powers (v**2) imply asymmetry or bias effects.
- A dominant -c0*v term indicates linear viscous damping and exponential decay of velocity in the absence of forcing.
- A -c0*v*Abs(v) term indicates speed-squared drag where dissipation increases strongly with |v| (often used as a turbulent/pressure-drag surrogate).
- A -c0*sign(v) or tanh(c*v) structure signals dry friction; near v=0 it can produce stick-slip-like behavior or sharp acceleration transitions.
- (c0 - c1*v**2)*v indicates negative damping at small |v| and positive damping at large |v|, a common mechanism for stable limit cycles (self-oscillation) in reduced models.
- Sin(c*t+phi) or cos(c*t+phi) additive terms represent external periodic forcing; frequencies inferred from c set the drive period.
- Time-periodic coefficients multiplying v (e.g., (c0+c1*cos(c2*t))*v) indicate parametric excitation or periodically varying damping (Mathieu-like mechanisms in a reduced coordinate).
- Localized exp(-c*(t-c0)**2) terms indicate transient impulses/kicks (e.g., impacts or short bursts), producing brief acceleration spikes.
- Polynomial dependence on t suggests slow drift in the operating point (e.g., changing setpoint, gravity component change, or ramped actuation) rather than a stationary oscillator.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1)

GT is the fixed function
\[
f(t,v)=0.782414626093252\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.0834249779987997\,v^3\;-\;0.995417005601056\,\log(|v|+1).
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Must contain a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no \(v\) inside), amplitude \(0.7824...\) (phase shift allowed via \(\sin(\omega t+\phi)\) but must reduce to \(\sin(t)\): need \(\omega=1\) and \(\phi=0\) mod \(2\pi\)).
- Must contain a \(-0.08342...\,v^3\) term (a power term with exponent 3).
- Must contain \(-0.9954...\log(|v|+1)\). **Absolute value is essential** (domain includes negative \(v\)); \(\log(c v+1)\) cannot equal \(\log(|v|+1)\) for all real \(v\).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO24)

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*log(Abs(v) + c1)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: -0.0834*v³ - 0.9954*log(|v| + 1) + 0.7824*sin(t)**

Key features of GT:
- A v³ term (odd power)
- A log(|v| + 1) term
- A sin(t) term
- No constant offset, no linear v term, no v² term, no exponential terms, no t-linear terms

Let me analyze each candidate systematically.

**Candidate 1:** c0*v² + c1*v^c2 + c3*sin(c4*v + c5) + c6 + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)
- Has v², v^c2, sin(v-dependent), sin(t). Missing log(|v|+1). sin(c4*v) cannot equal log(|v|+1). Set c0=0, c2=3, but sin(c4*v+c5) ≠ -log(|v|+1).
Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** c0 + c1*v^c2 + c3*exp(c4*v) + c5*log(c6*v + 1) + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)
- Set c2=3 for v³, c3=0 to kill exp, c8=1, c9=0 for sin(t). Then: c0 + c1*v³ + c5*log(c6*v+1) + c7*sin(t).
- GT has log(|v|+1). This has log(c6*v+1). When v < 0, log(c6*v+1) is defined only for v > -1/c6, but log(|v|+1) is always defined. These are different functions for negative v. log(|v|+1) = log(-v+1) for v<0, but log(c6*v+1) with any fixed c6 cannot match both log(v+1) for v>0 and log(-v+1) for v<0.
Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]
